Acta.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> We observed that the R<sub>ct</sub> values in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information) have the same range which can be explained by similar properties of the electrodes in the cells. Looking at the EIS elements in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information), we find that the highest W value is associated with the x = 0.4 Ru-substituted sample. This value is indicative of the diffusion rate of Na-ions within the system.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202406332-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202406332-sec-0050-title">2.3 Operando Structural Analysis</h3>
            
            <p><b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202406332-fig-0007">7a</a> shows the in situ XRD data of the cathode, Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ru<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> where x = 0.4, containing cells during the first two cycles. The strong peaks observed in the XRD data are due to the Al current collector. We focused on the (002), (004), (100), and (114) peak shifts during the cycling. During the charging process, the solid solution mechanism is revealed by the noticeable shift of the (004) peak toward lower angles and the (100) peak toward higher angles which the counter plot of this trend presented in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a> (Supporting Information). This trend corresponds to an expansion along the ‘c’ axis and a reduction along the ‘a’ axis. These lattice alterations occur during the removal of the sodium ions. As a result, a repulsive effect between the metal-oxide layers takes place instigating the expansion in the ‘c’ direction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0058_R_d233908592e2072" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Adv. Energy Mater.">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> At this stage, the active material displays a dual-phase region consisting of the P2 and OP4 phases. Upon further increasing the voltage to 4.3&nbsp;V, the structure completely transitions to the OP4 phase. We should indicate that the phase transitions between the P2 and OP4 phases during the charge and discharge process have a reversible property as obtained in the previous studies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0059_R_d233908592e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59">59</a>, <a href="#smll202406332-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0060_R_d233908592e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Chem. Mater.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It was observed that the intensity of the reflection planes in the XRD pattern is related to the OP4 phase. This phenomenon diminishes as the sodium content increases throughout the discharge process, eventually disappearing at ≈3.0&nbsp;V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0061_R_d233908592e2083" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> At the last stage of the discharge (down to 1.5&nbsp;V), the cell exhibits a more complex behavior, revealing a dual-phase region comprising the P2 and P2' (Cmcm) phases.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0062_R_d233908592e2088" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> When Na content is more than ≈0.8 per formula unit, the number of Mn<sup>3+</sup> ions increases triggering Jahn–Teller distortion that leads to a partial phase transition from P2 to P2’.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202406332-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/89f8a49f-5616-477a-9005-dc7ab27e271f/smll202406332-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/89f8a49f-5616-477a-9005-dc7ab27e271f/smll202406332-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/bcfb62d9-ff1c-4055-bb26-265cb3e706e2/smll202406332-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/89f8a49f-5616-477a-9005-dc7ab27e271f/smll202406332-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202406332-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202406332" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Structure evaluation of Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>0.6</sub>Ru<sub>0.4</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Ru substituted cathode during charge and discharge process with right panel showing phase transition from P2-OP4-Cmcm upon sodium extraction and re-insertion into the structure. The XAS spectrum of b) Mn K-edge and c) Ru K-edge depends on the charging and discharging process. The counter plot of FT of EXAFS for d) Mn and e) Ru K-edge during charge and discharge process of Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>1−x</sub>Ru<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> where x  =  0.4. The mapping data was calculated using OCV FT of XAS for Mn and Ru K-edge and it was subtracted from the FT of XAS graphs for different voltages.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>It is stated that the c-lattice parameters during the charging process (during Na+ extraction) increase and it is expected that the peak shift of (002) and (004) reflection planes to lower angles due to the repulsive electrostatic force between the neighboring oxygen layers. Peaks on a-b planes such as (112) or (114) reflection lines shift to higher angles because of the smaller ion radii of Mn at the valence state of 4+<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0063_R_d233908592e2135" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Chem. Sci.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which we also observed. Notice that the OP4 phase begins to appear after extracting 0.39&nbsp;mol Na<sup>+</sup> and persists until full charge, indicated by the characteristic OP4 (004) peak at 17.5° in the structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0064_R_d233908592e2142" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Nat. Mater.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>The in situ XAS studies were performed using a modified version of CR2032 coin cell where the cell allows X-ray penetration via the Kapton window.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0020_R_d233908592e2149" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Electrochim. Acta.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The XANES data was collected for the K edge of Mn and Ru elements for the x = 0.4 Ru substitution cathode active material during cycling. The XANES spectrums were presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202406332-fig-0007">7b,c</a>. It is evident that both Mn and Ru elements shifted toward higher energies during charging, indicating the oxidation of the Mn and Ru transition metals. This further advocates that these two elements contributed to the charge capacities. A clear peak position difference in the spectra of the Mn K-edge was observed between the XANES at OCV (6559.4&nbsp;eV) and the 4.3&nbsp;V charged (6560.9&nbsp;eV) electrodes in the cells. According to the reference data of Mn<sup>3+</sup>(Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>) and Mn<sup>4+</sup>(MnO<sub>2</sub>), the XANES peaks (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information) were observed at 6558.8 and 6561.2&nbsp;eV (showing an increase of 2.4&nbsp;eV in energy) for Mn<sup>3+</sup> and Mn<sup>4+</sup>, respectively. Therefore, it is clear that the Mn<sup>3+</sup> ions transform to Mn<sup>4+</sup>ions, albeit slightly lower oxidation state, during the charging process. The process is reversible as shown with the energy values in the XANES figure. The orange color in both Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202406332-fig-0007">7b,c</a> indicates that the data were recorded during rest, i.e., OCV. During charging the peak is gradually shifting higher energies and during the discharge the peak is shifting even below the OCV line as shown with purple color. The XANES peaks of Ru K-edge were given in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202406332-fig-0007">7c</a> and it is seen that the peaks for OCV and 4.3&nbsp;V were observed at 22&nbsp;132.8 and 22&nbsp;134.4&nbsp;eV, (showing an increase of 1.6&nbsp;eV in energy), respectively. The reference XANES data of Ru metal, Ru<sup>3+</sup> (RuCl<sup>3</sup>), and Ru<sup>4+</sup> (RuO<sub>2</sub>) were presented in literature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0065_R_d233908592e2195" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Nat. Commun.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The XANES data for OCV corresponds to Ru<sup>4+</sup> and the spectra of Ru K-edge gradually shifted to higher energies due to the oxidation of Ru ions from 4+ to 5+ as indicated in the literature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0065_R_d233908592e2203" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Nat. Commun.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It was previously calculated that the energy shifts values for SuRuO<sub>3</sub> and Sr<sub>2</sub>GdRuO<sub>6</sub> were found as 1.5&nbsp;eV stemming from the oxidation of Ru from 4+ to 5+.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0066_R_d233908592e2214" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - J. Supercond.">66</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Similar energy change was also found for our samples indicating oxidation state change from 4+ to 5+. Similar phenomena with respect to energy changes during charge and discharge were also seen in Ru however this change was much smaller than that of Mn. Because of this, we could not see the shift of the Ru peak back and forth as clearly as Mn one. To analyze the local structure around Mn and Ru ions in the x = 0.4 Ru-substituted containing half-cell, the Fourier Transform (FT) EXAFS maps from XAS data during galvanostatic measurements were generated using the Athena program. The results are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202406332-fig-0007">7d,e</a> as contour plots. The first and the second peaks in the corresponding EXAFS data reveals the metal-oxygen and metal–metal bonds, respectively. The bond lengths were calculated using the Artemis program. The fitting results at different cycles of the battery are plotted in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> (Supporting Information). The fitting parameters were optimized for each case in detail as reported in the literature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0067_R_d233908592e2226" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The P63/mmc symmetry was employed for the calculations, and the fitting of Mn and Ru was performed using the first scattering path of the data. The best-fit values of the structural parameters for OCV and 4.3 charged state are listed in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information). The symbol <i>N</i> represents the number of neighboring atoms, while the <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/204b11ec-67d0-4f56-a2d7-ee33b81aea3b/smll202406332-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202406332:smll202406332-math-0001" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202406332-math-0001.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>S</mi>
                        <mn>0</mn>
                        <mn>2</mn>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$S_0^2$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> denotes the amplitude reduction factor, typically found within the range of 0.7 &lt; <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/66da44a0-40bf-4465-90c7-67d369a70d90/smll202406332-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202406332:smll202406332-math-0002" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202406332-math-0002.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>S</mi>
                        <mn>0</mn>
                        <mn>2</mn>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$S_0^2$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> &lt; 1.0.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0064_R_d233908592e2255" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Nat. Mater.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the <i>R</i> (Å) is the radial distance to the neighboring atom, the <i>σ<sup>2</sup>(Å<sup>2</sup>)</i> is the mean-square disorder in <i>R</i>. The latter notion was named as Debye-Waller factor which is related to the correlation of atomic motion in the structure and can give information on the vibrational dynamics of the structure. This critical information can reveal the displacements of atoms from their idealized positions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0067_R_d233908592e2272" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The symbol <i>∆E</i> represents the energy difference between creating a photoelectron with energy <i>(E − E<sub>0</sub>)</i> where <i>E</i> is the energy of the incident X-ray that causes an atom to absorb, and <i>E<sub>0</sub></i> is the energy of the core electron that is destroyed. It should be noted that there could be different bond lengths for TM-O and TM-TM in the structure. According to Mn EXAFS data, the bond lengths of Mn-O, Mn–Mn, and Mn–Ru were calculated as 1.94, 2.89, and 3.20&nbsp;Å, respectively. This is expected because the repulsive force of Mn-Mn is lower than that of Mn–Ru in the structure. It was found in the literature that the Mn–O and Mn–Mn bond lengths for P2-type NaMnO<sub>2</sub> were calculated as 1.907 and 2.898&nbsp;Å, respectively which are close to the parameters we fitted at OCV.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0068_R_d233908592e2293" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - Sci. Rep.">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the similar substituted elements in the form of P2-NaMn<sub>0.9</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, it was found that the bond lengths were increased from 1.908 Å (Mn–O) and 2.901 Å (Mn–Mn) to 1.998 Å (Mn–O) and 2.905 (Mn–TM) by Fe doping.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0065_R_d233908592e2305" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Nat. Commun.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Since Fe and Ru are in the same column of the periodic table, we expected a similar outcome when doped into the same cathode. When the Na-ions are left from the lattice during the charging process, it is expected that Mn─O bonds decrease since the Na–O interaction is almost canceled in the structure. As for the bond lengths of the Mn–TM ions, it was observed that a stable structure existed for the bond structure, yielding improved stability of the lattice structure. Yabuuchi et. al. investigated the bond length of Fe–O in P2-type Na<sub>x</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode and they found that the bond length of Fe–O at pristine state was changed from 2 to 1.90&nbsp;Å when charged to 4.2&nbsp;V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0064_R_d233908592e2319" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Nat. Mater.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the Ru─O bond length was not affected during the charging and discharging process providing a more stable structure.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202406332-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202406332-sec-0060-title">2.4 Full-Cell Test Results</h3>
            
            <p>The full cells are assembled by using x = 0.3 and 0.4 Ru-substituted cathodes against commercial hard carbon anodes. We used a pre-sodiation technique for the anodes in which the details can be found in our previous papers.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0020_R_d233908592e2333" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Electrochim. Acta.">20</a>, <a href="#smll202406332-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0069_R_d233908592e2333" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Energy Technol.">69</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The cyclic voltammetry (CV) of the x = 0.3 and x = 0.4 Ru-substituted full cells is presented in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202406332-fig-0008">8a</a>. It is observed that there are four different redox peaks during the charging process, which were discussed in the half-cell section, previously. The redox peaks observed in the full cell also corroborate the data from the half-cell experiments. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202406332-fig-0008">8b,c</a> shows the voltage-capacity graphs of the cathode where x = 0.3 against hard carbon and the cathode where x = 0.4 against hard carbon full cells at different discharge rates. We utilized the following recipe for the cycle life assessment of the full cells as seen in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202406332-fig-0008">8d</a>: C/10 rate for 1 cycle, C/3 rate for 1 cycle, C/2 rate for 1 cycle, and 1C rate for 500 cycles. The obtained capacity values were presented in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information) and it is found that the first capacity for x = 0.3 and 0.4 full cells were obtained as 116 and 136&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and they were decreased to 66 and 86&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles, respectively.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202406332-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f02948ae-4edb-4a59-8ab7-43f8cbc3a673/smll202406332-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/f02948ae-4edb-4a59-8ab7-43f8cbc3a673/smll202406332-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/fdc2322b-c750-4547-8556-fde226f8b138/smll202406332-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f02948ae-4edb-4a59-8ab7-43f8cbc3a673/smll202406332-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202406332-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202406332" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV graphs, Voltage–capacity of Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ru<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> where b) x = 0.4 and c) x = 0.3, d) capacity-cycle number graphs up to 500 cycles and e) C-rate data of the full-cells for x = 0.3 and x = 0.4.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The capacity retention values for 500 cycles were obtained as 57% and 67% for x = 0.3 and x = 0.4 full cells, respectively. Obtaining close to 70% capacity retention after 500 cycles at 100% DOD in a sodium ion full cell is outstanding. It is evident from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202406332-fig-0008">8e</a> that the cells containing cathode where x = 0.4 exhibits better performance at 1C rate. However, high current rates can lead to increased capacity loss for the cells containing cathode where x = 0.4. We also evaluated the rate dependency of the cells containing cathode where x = 0.3 and x = 0.4. The cell containing the cathode where x = 0.4 exhibited better full-cell performance compared to the cell containing the cathode where x = 0.3. Although there is an impurity phase of Na<sub>2</sub>RuO<sub>3</sub> for x≥0.4, it should be noted that the capacitive contribution for x = 0.4 is higher than that of x = 0.3, which could enhance the battery performance of the cells. The EIS analysis of the full cells is given in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information) and the fitting model is presented in the inset of the Figure. In this study, the EIS, as illustrated in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information), revealing four distinctive regions diverging from the EIS profile of the half-cell. The initial region (I) exhibiting lower impedance corresponds to the ohmic component, while the subsequent small semicircle (region II) arises from the surface film resistance. Regions III and IV are associated with the cathode and anode, respectively, and the final linear segment at lower frequencies indicates mass transfer phenomena within the cells.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0060_R_d233908592e2403" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Chem. Mater.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The corresponding fitting parameters are tabulated in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). Notably, the stark contrast between the full-cell and half-cell EIS profiles is attributed to differences in cell configuration. Interactions between the anode (hard carbon) and Ru-doped cathode give rise to the processes like side reactions, shuttle effects, or alterations in electrolyte composition, thereby affecting the impedance profile. Moreover, in the full-cell setup, the kinetics of both anodic and cathodic reactions can influence the overall impedance response. This can result in different profiles compared to the half-cell configuration, where typically kinetics of only one of the electrodes are a contributing factor. Moreover, differences in the geometry of the full-cell and half-cell setups, including electrode dimensions, shape, and inter-electrode spacing, can affect the distribution of current and potential gradients within the cell. These geometric differences can change the impedance response by modulating the distribution of electrochemical processes and charge transfer kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0061_R_d233908592e2411" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">61</a>, <a href="#smll202406332-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0044_R_d233908592e2411" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Carbon Energy.">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The initial region (R<sub>s</sub> in EQC) exhibiting lower impedance corresponds to the ohmic component, while the subsequent small semicircle (R<sub>1</sub> and Q<sub>1</sub> in EQC) arises from surface film resistance. The impedance associated with the cathode and anode corresponds to R<sub>2</sub>/Q<sub>2</sub> and R<sub>3</sub>/O<sub>3</sub> in EQC, respectively, and the final linear segment at lower frequencies indicates mass transfer phenomena within the cells. The corresponding fitting parameters are detailed in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information).</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202406332-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202406332-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>We have investigated the role of Ru in enhancing the cycling capability of the Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>0.5-x</sub>RuO<sub>2</sub> cathode active material. The detailed XRD analysis along with the fitting results confirm that when Ru doping is below x = 0.5, the Ru doping does not reveal any structural impurities. A change in the lattice volume as a function of increasing Ru content is attributed to the different ionic radii for different coordination and valance states of the ions which was supported by the FTIR and Raman spectroscopy measurements. Through in situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) and X-ray diffraction (XRD) studies, we have unraveled the role of Ru in the lattice structure. Magnetization calculations revealed the presence of stronger Ru─O bonds and the stabilizing effect of Ru-doping on MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedra within the structure. Density of States (DOS) calculations showed that the bandgap of NMO reduced by Ru doping leading to the enhancement of the electronic conductivity of the pure NMO cathode. The performance of the full cell containing Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>0.6</sub>Ru<sub>0.4</sub>O<sub>2</sub>/ Hard Carbon delivered an outstanding battery performance where 67% capacity retention was obtained after 500 cycles at 100% DOD.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202406332-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202406332-sec-0080-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <p>Na<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, RuO<sub>2</sub>, and MnO<sub>2</sub> were used as the starting materials to synthesize Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>1–x</sub>Ru<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> where x varied between 0.05 and 0.5. The initial precursors were mixed using an agate mortar for ≈2&nbsp;h and pressed to form the pellet under 5 tons of pressure. The Ru-substituted pellets were annealed at 900&nbsp;°C for 5 h in an ambient atmosphere and quenched using L-N<sub>2</sub>. After the annealing, the samples were kept in a glove box where oxygen and moisture levels were under 5&nbsp;ppm. X-ray diffraction analysis was performed using a Malvern Panalytical EMPYREAN (3rd generation) diffractometer, employing a CuK<sub>α</sub> (λ<sub>Kα</sub> = 1.5405&nbsp;Å). GSAS-II software was used to analyze the structural parameters.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0070" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0070_R_d233908592e2495" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 70 - Powder Diffr.">70</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Fourier transform infrared (FTIR) data was collected using a Perkin Elmer Spectrum One spectrophotometer. The spectrophotometer was equipped with NRS-4500 Confocal Raman Microscope with a 532&nbsp;nm laser located at AYBU-MERLAB, Ankara, Türkiye. Surface morphology and elemental mapping were analyzed using a Thermo Fisher Scientific Apreo Scanning Electron Microscope (SEM) combined with an energy-dispersive X-ray (EDS) unit (Thermo Scientific Ultra Dry Detector). Thermo Scientific K-Alpha system with a monochromatic Al-Kα source was used for the XPS analysis located at EMUM-Izmir-Turkey (Detail can be found in ref. [<span><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0071_R_d233908592e2499" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Vacuum.">71</a></span>]</p>
         
         <p>The CR2032 cells were fabricated using the blend of the active material, Super-P carbon, and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) (with a weight ratio of 70:15:15) and were suspended with the proper amount of <i>N</i>-Metyl-2-Pyrrolidone (NMP). The mixture was coated on Al foil using a doctor blade, and later kept in a vacuum furnace at 110&nbsp;°C for 24 h for drying. The electrodes were punched with 15&nbsp;mm diameter discs. Na-foil and 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> (PC/EC = 50/50, w/w) were used as anode and electrolyte, respectively, to assemble CR2032 half-cells. Cyclic voltammetry measurements were conducted between 1.5 and 4.3&nbsp;V with a scan rate of 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. Neware BTS4000 and Hefa-cycle BA100A battery analyzers were utilized for charging and discharging the cells. The electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) test was run from 0.1&nbsp;mHz to 200&nbsp;kHz using 10&nbsp;mV AC amplitude voltage. A full cell containing Ru-doped cathode against a hard carbon anode was also assembled. The details of fabrication and electrochemical characterizations of the full cells are documented in the previous study.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0069_R_d233908592e2514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Energy Technol.">69</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To enhance the capacity of the cells, a pre-sodiation strategy was employed, and the galvanostatic discharge–charge–discharge method was used for the pre-sodiation process. Ru-substituted cathode and pre-sodiated hard carbon (provided by Gelon Limited) were assembled in CR2032 coin cells.</p>
         
         <p>X-ray absorption near-edge (XANES) and extended x-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) analysis were performed at XAS/XRF Beamline at SESAME located in Allen, Jordan. The fluorescence mode of the beamline was used to collect the XANES/EXAFS data at the Mn, and Ru K-edges at room temperature. Mn and Ru foils were used for calibration and alignment purposes before the data collection. After the calibration and alignment, XAS measurements were recorded during cycling between a voltage window of 1.5–4.3&nbsp;V at a 30&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> rate. Details of the cell design in this study can be found in the previous study.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0020_R_d233908592e2525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Electrochim. Acta.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Analysis of the XAS data was performed by the Athena and Artemis program.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0072_R_d233908592e2530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - Phys. Scr.">72</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>A time-resolved X-ray Diffraction (TR-XRD) instrument was used for in situ XRD measurements at the Korea Institute of Science and Technology located in South Korea. The initial and final angles of the XRD were set to 10°–90°, and the data were collected at 180&nbsp;s intervals for each scan during the measurement. For the TOF-SIMS studies, an ION-TOF (Münster) was used, where the pressure of the analysis chamber was maintained below 2&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−9</sup>&nbsp;mbar to produce an ultrahigh vacuum. All the detected secondary ions of interest possessed negative polarity. A pulsed 30&nbsp;keV Bi<sup>3+</sup>-ion beam was applied for the spectrum and depth profiling. For sputtering the cathode material, a 3&nbsp;keV Cs<sup>+</sup>-ion beam was used with a typical sputtered area of 200&nbsp;×&nbsp;200&nbsp;µm. Atomic-scale high-angle annular dark field transmission electron microscope (HAADF-TEM) images, along with STEM and HR-TEM images and SAED patterns were investigated by using an FEI Titan TM 80−300 microscope at 300&nbsp;kV.</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">Density functional theory (DFT) calculations were conducted using the Vienna Ab initio Simulation Package (VASP) using projector augmented wave (PAW) method.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0073_R_d233908592e2547" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">73</a>-<a href="#smll202406332-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0076_R_d233908592e2547" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - Phys. Rev. B.">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Spin-polarized generalized gradient approximation (GGA) was employed with Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof (PBE) exchange-correlation functional with DFT+U correction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0077" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0077_R_d233908592e2552" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 77 - Phys. Rev. Lett.">77</a>, <a href="#smll202406332-bib-0078" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0078_R_d233908592e2552" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 78 - Phys. Rev. B.">78</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To account for the Coulomb interaction between <i>d</i>-orbital electrons of transition metals, Hubbard U parameters of 4.95 and 5&nbsp;eV for Mn and Ru atoms were applied, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0079" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0079_R_d233908592e2560" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 79 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">79</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electron configurations of Na (2p<sup>6</sup>3s<sup>1</sup>), Mn (3p<sup>6</sup>4s<sup>2</sup>3d<sup>10</sup>), Ru (4p<sup>6</sup>5s<sup>2</sup>4d<sup>10</sup>) and O (2s<sup>2</sup>2p<sup>4</sup>) were treated as the valence electrons. A conjugate gradient algorithm was used for ionic relaxation with a plane wave cutoff energy of 520&nbsp;eV. For the electronic relaxation, Gaussian smearing with a width of 0.05&nbsp;eV was used. The convergence criteria for electronic and ionic relaxations were set to 10–5&nbsp;eV and 0.03&nbsp;eV&nbsp;Å<sup>−1</sup> respectively. The Brillouin zone was sampled using an automatic k-point mesh with a Gamma-centered grid of 2 × 4 × 2. The initial structures of both Na<sub>0.675</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> (NMO) and Na<sub>0.675</sub>Mn<sub>0.6</sub>Ru<sub>0.4</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Ru-NMO) are derived from Rietveld refinements of X-ray diffraction (XRD) data. The supercell program is used to create supercells of 4 × 2 × 1 with varying Na content over a full range of 0 ≤ Na<sub>𝑥</sub> ≤ 1 and to address the partial occupancy of Mn/Ru in the crystal structure of Ru-NMO.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0080" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0080_R_d233908592e2604" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 80 - J. Cheminform.">80</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electrostatic energies of the generated supercell are calculated using the Ewald summation method, as implemented in pymatgen library.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202406332-bib-0081" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0081_R_d233908592e2609" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 81 - Comput. Phys. Commun.">81</a>, <a href="#smll202406332-bib-0082" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202406332-bib-0082_R_d233908592e2609" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 82 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">82</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The generated supercells of NMO and Ru-NMO are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information). The formation energy was calculated using the below equation where <i>E</i> refers to the total energy of the system.

        <script type="text/javascript" nonce="098a36503a7f4fa0a1a6f4302eb73e48">
    window.addEventListener('load', () => {
        document.querySelectorAll('.admin-bar-popup-menu ul li')?.forEach(function (li) {
            const anchor = li.querySelector('a');
            if (anchor && anchor.textContent.trim() === 'Edit Access Denial') {
                li.style.display = 'none';
            }
        });
